# KR2 (Krokinobacter eikastus Rhodopsin 2) — Light-Driven Sodium Pump

<div class="expr-badges"><span class="expr-badge expr-e-coli">E. coli</span> <span class="expr-badge expr-p-pastoris">P. pastoris</span></div>


<a class="badge badge-uniprot" href="https://www.uniprot.org/uniprot/N0DKS8">UniProt: N0DKS8</a>

<span class="expr-badge">Dokdonia eikasta</span>

## Overview

KR2 (Krokinobacter eikastus rhodopsin 2) is a light-driven sodium-pumping rhodopsin and the first discovered light-driven non-proton cation pump. It was identified from the marine flavobacterium Krokinobacter eikastus and represents the founding member of a new class of [Microbial Rhodopsins](/xray-mp-wiki/concepts/rhodopsin-mechanisms/microbial-rhodopsins/). The 2015 Nature paper (Kato et al.) reported the first crystal structures of KR2 under acidic (pH 4.0) and neutral (pH ~8.0) conditions at 2.3 A resolution, revealing the structural basis for Na+ transport. KR2 contains the characteristic NDQ motif (Asn112, Asp116, Gln123) that distinguishes Na+-pumping rhodopsins from proton-pumping rhodopsins. The gating mechanism involves flipping of Asp116 upon protonation to sequester the Schiff base proton from the conducting pathway, thereby facilitating Na+ transport. Structure-based engineering produced the first light-driven K+ pump (KR2_K+, N61P/G263W). KR2 has been demonstrated as an inhibitory optogenetics tool in mammalian cortical neurons and C. elegans. A 2019 structure (Kovalev et al.) revealed the pentameric form at 2.2 A under physiological pH 8.0, demonstrating that pentamerization is essential for Na+-pumping activity, and that the switch from Na+- to H+-pumping at acidic pH corresponds to an expanded-to-compact conformational change. A later 2020 structure captured the O-intermediate state of the pentameric form at 2.1 A (PDB 6XYT), revealing direct sodium coordination by the NDQ triad.

**Expression:**

- **Expression system**: Escherichia coli C41(DE3); also Pichia pastoris not used for this construct
- **Construct**: KR2 gene (GI: 478430804) from K. eikastus (NBRC 100814), cloned into pET-modified vector with TEV cleavage site followed by His8 tag at C terminus. For spectroscopic experiments, a synthesized gene with codons optimized for E. coli expression was used. H30L, H30K, Y154F, S254A, G263F mutants generated by site-directed mutagenesis.

**Purification:**

- **Expression system**: Not specified
- **Tag info**: Not specified

### doi/10.1038##nature14322

**Structures:**

  <thead><tr>
    <th>PDB ID</th>
    <th>Resolution</th>
    <th>Space Group</th>
    <th>Construct</th>
    <th>Ligand/Co-factor</th>
  </tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td><a class="pdb-link" href="https://www.rcsb.org/structure/3x3b">3X3B</a></td>
      <td>2.3</td>
      <td>I222</td>
      <td>Full-length KR2 from Krokinobacter eikastus (residues 5-275), with C-terminal TEV cleavage site and His8 tag, crystallized under acidic conditions (pH 4.0)</td>
      <td>All-trans <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/retinal/">Retinal</a> (ATR), three lipids (putative), one <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/peg/">PEG</a></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><a class="pdb-link" href="https://www.rcsb.org/structure/3x3b">3X3B</a></td>
      <td>2.3</td>
      <td>I222</td>
      <td>Full-length KR2 from Krokinobacter eikastus (residues 5-275), with C-terminal TEV cleavage site and His8 tag, crystallized under neutral conditions (pH 7.5-8.5, by soaking crystals at pH 4.0 in pH 8.0-9.0 buffer)</td>
      <td>All-trans <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/retinal/">Retinal</a> (ATR), three lipids</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
 - R-work 0.2072%, R-free 0.2486%; Data collection: Acidic condition (pH 4.0), representing M-like intermediate state. Wavelength 1.0 A. Cell dimensions a=40.6, b=81.6, c=233.8 A
 - R-work 0.1949%, R-free 0.2308%; Data collection: Neutral condition (pH 7.5-8.5), representing resting state. Wavelength 1.0 A. Cell dimensions a=40.6, b=83.5, c=234.6 A

**Expression:**

- **Expression system**: Escherichia coli C41(DE3); also Pichia pastoris not used for this construct
- **Construct**: KR2 gene (GI: 478430804) from K. eikastus (NBRC 100814), cloned into pET-modified vector with TEV cleavage site followed by His8 tag at C terminus. For spectroscopic experiments, a synthesized gene with codons optimized for E. coli expression was used. H30L, H30K, Y154F, S254A, G263F mutants generated by site-directed mutagenesis.

**Purification:**

- **Expression system**: [E. coli](/xray-mp-wiki/concepts/methods-techniques/c41-e-coli-expression-strain/) C41(DE3)
- **Expression construct**: Full-length KR2 (GI: 478430804) with C-terminal [TEV](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/tev-protease/)-His8 tag
- **Tag info**: C-terminal His8 tag, removed by [TEV protease](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/tev-protease/) after [Ni-NTA](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) [Affinity Chromatography](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/affinity-chromatography/)

<table class="wiki-table">
  <thead><tr>
    <th>Step</th>
    <th>Method</th>
    <th>Resin / Column</th>
    <th>Buffer + Detergent</th>
    <th>Notes</th>
  </tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td>Expression</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/iptg/">IPTG</a> induction</td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>-- + --</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/concepts/methods-techniques/c41-e-coli-expression-strain/">E. coli</a> C41(DE3) cells induced with 0.5 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/iptg/">IPTG</a> and supplemented with 10 uM all-trans <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/retinal/">Retinal</a>, expressed for 3 h at 37 C</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Cell disruption and membrane collection</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/ultracentrifugation/">Ultracentrifugation</a></td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>50 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris-HCl Buffer</a> (pH 8.0), 300 mM NaCl, 20 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/imidazole/">Imidazole</a> + 1.5% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a></td>
      <td>Cells disrupted and membrane fraction collected by <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/ultracentrifugation/">ultracentrifugation</a> at 125,000g for 1 h. Solubilization buffer also contained 0.1 mM PMSF and 0.3% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">[CHS</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/)</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/affinity-chromatography/">Affinity Chromatography</a></td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) affinity</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/)</td>
      <td>50 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris-HCl Buffer</a> (pH 8.0), 300 mM NaCl, 20 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/imidazole/">Imidazole</a> + 1.5% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a>, 0.3% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">[CHS</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/)</td>
      <td>Protein solubilized with <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a>/<a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">[CHS</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/), bound to <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) resin, eluted with <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/imidazole/">Imidazole</a> gradient</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Tag cleavage and dialysis</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/tev-protease/">TEV</a> protease cleavage</td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>50 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris-HCl Buffer</a> (pH 8.0), 150 mM NaCl + 0.02% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a>, 0.004% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">[CHS</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/)</td>
      <td>After <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/), fractions treated with <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/tev-protease/">TEV</a> protease and dialyzed against buffer A overnight</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Second <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">Ni-NTA</a> (negative purification)</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) flow-through</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/)</td>
      <td>50 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris-HCl Buffer</a> (pH 8.0), 150 mM NaCl + 0.02% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a>, 0.004% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">[CHS</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/)</td>
      <td>Cleaved His8 tag and <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/tev-protease/">TEV</a> protease removed by passing through <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) resin, collecting flow-through</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Gel filtration</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/">[SEC</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/)</td>
      <td>Gel filtration column</td>
      <td>50 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris-HCl Buffer</a> (pH 8.0) + 0.05% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a>, 0.01% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">[CHS</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/)</td>
      <td>Purified further by gel-filtration chromatography. Final protein concentrated to 20 mg/ml using 100 kDa MWCO centrifugal filter</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
**Final sample**: 20 mg/ml purified KR2 in 50 mM [Tris-HCl Buffer](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/) (pH 8.0), 0.05% [DDM](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/), 0.01% [CHS](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/)

    <tr>
      <td>Growth time</td>
      <td>Not specified</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Cryoprotection</td>
      <td>Crystals harvested directly from <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/crystallization/lipidic-cubic-phase/">LCP</a> matrix using MiTeGen microwouts, flash-cooled in liquid nitrogen</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Notes</td>
      <td>Crystals grown using mosquito <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/crystallization/lipidic-cubic-phase/">LCP</a> robot (TTP LabTech), 50-100 nl protein-<a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/crystallization/lipidic-cubic-phase/">LCP</a> mixture overlaid with 800-1000 nl precipitant. Initially obtained from MemMeso screen (Molecular Dimensions). For neutral conditions, soaking buffer (42% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/peg/">PEG</a> 200, 0.1 M <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris-HCl Buffer</a> pH 8.0-9.0, 0.05 M MgCl2) was added to well containing pH 4.0 crystals; final pH 7.5-8.5. Structures solved by <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/molecular-replacement/">Molecular Replacement</a> using XR (PDB 3DDL) as search model.</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: Na+-pumping form at physiological pH 8.0. Ground state of pentameric KR2.
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: pH 5.0 structure showing mixed expanded/compact conformations. Asp116 protonated, distance to RSB increased to 3.2 A.
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: pH 6.0 structure — same as pH 8.0, KR2 remains in Na+-pumping expanded conformation
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: Dry form — all protomers in compact conformation, identical to PDB 4XTO
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: Wet form — protomers switch back to expanded conformation after rehydration
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: Y154F mutant — pentamerization disrupted, Na+ pumping notably decreased
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: H30K mutant — pentamerization disrupted, Na+ pumping notably decreased
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: S254A mutant — shown to pump K+ in addition to Na+ and H+
 - R-work Not specified%, R-free Not specified%; Data collection: G263F mutant — shown to pump K+

**Expression:**

- **Expression system**: Escherichia coli C41(DE3); also Pichia pastoris not used for this construct
- **Construct**: KR2 gene (GI: 478430804) from K. eikastus (NBRC 100814), cloned into pET-modified vector with TEV cleavage site followed by His8 tag at C terminus. For spectroscopic experiments, a synthesized gene with codons optimized for E. coli expression was used. H30L, H30K, Y154F, S254A, G263F mutants generated by site-directed mutagenesis.

**Purification:**

- **Expression system**: [E. coli](/xray-mp-wiki/concepts/methods-techniques/c41-e-coli-expression-strain/) C41(DE3)
- **Expression construct**: Full-length KR2 (GI: 478430804) with C-terminal His8 tag
- **Tag info**: C-terminal 8xHis tag (not removed, used for [Ni-NTA](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) purification)

<table class="wiki-table">
  <thead><tr>
    <th>Step</th>
    <th>Method</th>
    <th>Resin / Column</th>
    <th>Buffer + Detergent</th>
    <th>Notes</th>
  </tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td>Expression</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/iptg/">IPTG</a> induction</td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>-- + --</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/concepts/methods-techniques/c41-e-coli-expression-strain/">E. coli</a> C41(DE3) cells transformed with pET-modified vector containing KR2 with C-terminal His8 tag. Expression induced with <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/iptg/">IPTG</a>, supplemented with all-trans <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/retinal/">Retinal</a>.</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Cell lysis</td>
      <td>High-pressure homogenization and <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/ultracentrifugation/">ultracentrifugation</a></td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>50 mM NaH2PO4/Na2HPO4 (pH 8.0), 0.1 M NaCl + --</td>
      <td>Cells resuspended in buffer with DNase I and lysozyme. Membrane fraction isolated by <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/ultracentrifugation/">ultracentrifugation</a> at 90,000g for 1 h at 4 C</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Solubilization</td>
      <td>Detergent extraction</td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>50 mM NaH2PO4/Na2HPO4 (pH 8.0), 0.1 M NaCl + 1% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a></td>
      <td>Membrane pellet resuspended and stirred overnight for solubilization. Insoluble fraction removed by <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/ultracentrifugation/">ultracentrifugation</a></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">Ni-NTA</a> affinity</td>
      <td>Immobilized metal <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/affinity-chromatography/">Affinity Chromatography</a></td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) (Qiagen)</td>
      <td>50 mM NaH2PO4/Na2HPO4 (pH 7.5), 0.1 M NaCl, 0.5 M <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/imidazole/">Imidazole</a> + 0.1% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a></td>
      <td>Supernatant loaded on <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/">[Ni-NTA</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/nickel-nta/) column, eluted with <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/imidazole/">Imidazole</a> gradient</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/">Size-Exclusion Chromatography</a></td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/">[SEC</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/)</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/superdex-200/">Superdex 200</a> prep grade (125 ml, GE Healthcare)</td>
      <td>50 mM NaH2PO4/Na2HPO4 (pH 7.5), 0.1 M NaCl + 0.05% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a></td>
      <td>Eluate subjected to <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/">[SEC</a>](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/). Fractions with minimal A280/A525 ratio pooled and concentrated to 60 mg/ml for crystallization</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
**Final sample**: 60 mg/ml purified KR2 in 50 mM NaH2PO4/Na2HPO4 (pH 7.5), 0.1 M NaCl, 0.05% [DDM](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/)

**Crystallization:**

<table class="wiki-kv-table">
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td>Method</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/crystallization/lipidic-cubic-phase/">In meso</a> (<a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/crystallization/lipidic-cubic-phase/">LCP</a> / <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/lipids/monoolein/">Monoolein</a>)</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Protein sample</td>
      <td>Purified KR2 at 25 mg/ml in 50 mM NaH2PO4/Na2HPO4 (pH 7.5), 0.1 M NaCl, 0.05% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Lipid</td>
      <td>Monooleoyl-formed lipidic phase (Nu-Chek Prep)</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Protein-to-lipid ratio</td>
      <td>Not specified</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Temperature</td>
      <td>22 C</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Growth time</td>
      <td>2-4 weeks</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Cryoprotection</td>
      <td>Not specified</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Notes</td>
      <td>Crystals grown using NT8 robotic system (Formulatrix). Blue crystals obtained at pH 4.3, red crystals at pH 8.0. For pH-soaking experiments, crystals grown at pH 8.0 were transferred to 3.4 M <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/sodium-malonate/">Sodium Malonate</a> baths at desired pH and equilibrated iteratively over 48+ hours. For monomeric form studies, crystals grown at pH 4.3 were soaked at pH 4.3, 6.0, and 8.0. Dry form obtained by fishing crystals without additional buffer; wet form by re-adding buffer and equilibrating for 30 min.</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

## Biological / Functional Insights

### NDQ triad coordinates sodium ion near retinal Schiff base

The O-intermediate structure (PDB 6XYT) revealed a sodium ion bound near the [Retinal](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/retinal/) Schiff base, coordinated by N112 and D116 of the characteristic NDQ triad. This was the first direct observation of sodium inside the KR2 protein, providing the structural basis for understanding the sodium-pumping mechanism. The NDQ triad is a conserved motif in sodium-pumping rhodopsins that distinguishes them from proton-pumping rhodopsins.

### Sodium release pathway via Q78

Metadynamics simulations and pumping activity measurements of putative pathway mutants demonstrated that sodium release likely proceeds alongside Q78 towards the structural sodium ion bound between KR2 protomers. This defines a complete ion translocation pathway through the protein.

### Pentameric assembly is critical for sodium pump function

The pentameric form of KR2 is the physiologically relevant assembly. The structural sodium ion bound between protomers is essential for function, highlighting the importance of oligomeric assembly for ion pump activity. Mutations that affect pentamer formation also impair sodium pumping.

### Potential for optogenetic tool engineering

KR2 is the only non-proton cation active transporter with demonstrated potential for optogenetics. The detailed structural understanding of the sodium transport mechanism, including the O-intermediate state, NDQ triad coordination, and release pathway, provides a basis for rational engineering of enhanced optogenetic tools with altered ion selectivity or pumping characteristics.

### Asp116 flipping gate mechanism for Na+ transport

The 2015 Nature paper (Kato et al.) established the gating mechanism for Na+ transport. In the resting state, the protonated Schiff base nitrogen is located in the centre of the ion transport pathway, preventing cation transport by electrostatic repulsion. After [Retinal](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/retinal/) photoisomerization and N-H flipping, the Schiff base proton is transferred to Asp116 (during the K-to-M intermediate transition). The protonated Asp116 then flips away from the Schiff base and forms hydrogen bonds with Ser70 and Asn112, moving the positive charge away from the centre of the pathway. This flipping reduces the energy barrier to Na+ transport and facilitates Na+ conduction. In the O intermediate, the proton re-associates with the Schiff base, preventing reverse flow of Na+. This model is supported by mutagenesis: D116N completely abolished Na+ transport; S70A and N112A mutants lost Na+ transport activity; while S70T and N112D retained activity, confirming the importance of the hydrogen bonding network for fixing the protonated Asp116 conformation.

### Engineering of first light-driven K+ pump (KR2_K+)

Based on the gating model, since Asp116 flipping does not actively select Na+ but only facilitates non-proton cation transfer, it was possible to engineer KR2 variants with altered ion selectivity. Focusing on residues Asn61 and Gly263 forming the intracellular vestibule, the double mutation N61P/G263W (KR2_K+) was found to preferentially transfer K+ over Na+ (K+/Na+ selectivity ratio 1.17 +/- 0.15). Since intracellular K+ concentration is approximately ten times higher than Na+, KR2_K+ is expected to work efficiently as a K+ pump in vivo. This represents the first engineered light-driven K+ pump.

### KR2 as an inhibitory optogenetics tool

KR2 functions as an inhibitory optogenetics tool. In rat cortical neurons, KR2 activation with green light (530-600 nm, 5.4 mW/mm2) produced outward photocurrents that hyperpolarized the membrane potential and inhibited action potential firing. The photocurrent was voltage-independent and stable for over one minute. In C. elegans, pan-neuronal expression of KR2-Venus slowed forward locomotion upon green light illumination, confirming the inhibitory effect at the behavioural level. Unlike [Halorhodopsin (HR) from Halobacterium salinarum](/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/rhodopsins/halorhodopsin/) (HR) and [AR3](/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/rhodopsins/archaerhodopsin-3/) ([AR3](/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/rhodopsins/archaerhodopsin-3/)), KR2 does not induce pH-sensitive channel side effects, and the outward flow of Na+ is more physiological than H+ or Cl- transport.

### Pentameric KR2 structure at physiological pH reveals Na+-pumping form

The 2019 structure of KR2 at pH 8.0 (2.2 A) revealed the protein in its functional pentameric form. In contrast to earlier monomeric structures from crystals grown at acidic pH, the pentameric form at physiological pH orients the protein nearly perpendicular to the membrane plane, with the ion uptake cavity positioned in the hydrophilic part. The structure shows a large Schiff base cavity filled with four water molecules. The Asp116 orientation is uniform within the pentameric assembly. The expanded conformation of the Schiff base region differs considerably from the compact conformation seen in low-pH monomeric structures.

### Structural basis of Na+-to-H+ pump switch with pH

KR2 switches from Na+ pumping at pH 6.0-8.0 to H+ pumping at pH 4.3. The pH 5.0 structure (2.6 A) revealed that Asn112 and Leu74 occupy two alternative conformations — the expanded conformation (Na+-pumping form at pH 8.0) and the compact conformation (H+-pumping form). The Asp116-Schiff base distance increases from 2.8 A (pH 8.0) to 3.2 A (pH 5.0), indicating Asp116 protonation. The compact conformation of KR2 corresponds to the H+-pumping form while the expanded conformation corresponds to the Na+-pumping form. The switch between these conformations is therefore the structural basis of the pH-dependent functional switch.

### Pentamerization is essential for KR2 Na+-pumping activity

Mutations at the oligomerization interface (H30L, H30K, Y154F) demonstrate a strong correlation between oligomeric state and ion-pumping activity. SEC profiles show that at pH 8.0, H30K and Y154F mutants form negligible pentameric assembly, while H30L is unstable and aggregates. Na+ pumping activity is notably decreased for H30K and Y154F, and completely absent for H30L. Crystal structures of H30K (1.8 A) and Y154F (2.2 A) confirm they form monomers in the asymmetric unit, identical to the wild-type monomeric form. HS-AFM studies show KR2 forms pentamers in lipid bilayers at both pH 8.0 and 4.3, not monomers.

### Dehydration causes compact conformation in KR2 crystals

Crystals that dried out during fishing switched from red to purple color and from expanded to compact conformation. The dry form structure (3.0 A, identical to PDB 4XTO from earlier work) has all protomers in compact conformation, while rehydrating the crystals for 30 min restored the expanded conformation and red color. This explains discrepancies between earlier structural studies and underscores the importance of humidity control during crystal growth and fishing.

- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/rhodopsins/archaerhodopsin-2/">Archaerhodopsin-2</a> — Related light-driven proton pump from archaebacteria
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/rhodopsins/pharaonis-halorhodopsin/">Pharaonis Halorhodopsin</a> — Related light-driven ion pump; comparison of Cl- vs Na+ transport mechanism
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/rhodopsins/sensory-rhodopsin-ii/">Sensory Rhodopsin II</a> — Related microbial rhodopsin from Natronomonas pharaonis
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/rhodopsins/channelrhodopsin-c1c2/">Channelrhodopsin C1C2</a> — Related optogenetic tool; comparison of light-activated ion transport
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/retinal/">Retinal</a> — Chromophore essential for light-driven sodium pumping; all-trans retinal bound via protonated Schiff base to Lys242
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/crystallization/lipidic-cubic-phase/">Lipidic Cubic Phase (LCP) Crystallization</a> — Crystallization method used for KR2 structure determination
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/n-dodecyl-beta-d-maltoside/">n-Dodecyl-beta-D-Maltoside (DDM)</a> — Primary solubilization and purification detergent for KR2
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">Cholesteryl Hemisuccinate (CHS)</a> — Used as stabilizing additive throughout KR2 purification and in final sample buffer
- <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/concepts/rhodopsin-mechanisms/microbial-rhodopsins/">Microbial Rhodopsins</a> — Related biological concept
